  733. I have to admit I was more than a little excited to try this fiber last mascara, this was provided to me as a sample for review. It has taken over the beauty world and given an entire new twist to mascara and fake lashes (Which I am never able to apply appropriately so I do not wear them). My lashes are already a decent length but I definitely could use thickness, which I was hoping to achieve with the fiber lash mascara. What an amazing difference it made! But, it is a good learning process like a winged liner, so here is my learning curve.<br /><br />It's a bit tricky at first & I got frustrated to figure out how to get beautiful lashes and no flakiness. So I followed the directions to the letter and then I was not disappointed.<br /><br />Tips for a fail proof method:<br /><br />1) Do one eye at a time. This is essential because you apply the gel then quickly apply the fibers while the gel is still wet, wait about 20 seconds for the fibers to set then apply the gel again to seal in the fibers. The sequence is gel-fibers-gel.<br />2) You can repeat these steps as often as you wish to get the desired effect. I find 2 total coats of the system gives me the look I want.<br />3) One hint from my own experience - I find it helps to apply one coat of your regular mascara first before you begin the gel/fiber application then seal everything with a final coat of regular mascara. It helps keep the fibers locked in. My routine is regular mascara - gel - fibers - gel - fibers - gel - regular mascara.<br />4) This removes easily with soapy facial cleanser and water provided you're not using a waterproof mascara to seal the whole deal down. If using a waterproof mascara then use some coconut oil or cleanser that melts the waterproof mascara and wash off everything.

  813. To accurately use these &#34;fiber&#34; mascaras you do the following:<br /><br />1) take a small cup and put very hot water in it. Place the transplanting gel tube into cup<br />2) apply your normal mascara. This serves as a base coat and works wonders<br />3) open the fibers tube and then grab the transplanting gel from hot water<br />4) apply transplanting gel to lashes. Be sure to coat good.<br />5) apply fibers.<br />6) wait about 45 seconds for fibers to gel not lashes<br />7) apply one more coat of transplanting gel to set the fibers (this will prevent fall out)<br /><br />I will then put the lid back on gel and place back into hot water, let my lashes set approx. 90 seconds and then repeat steps 3-7 again. This helps intensfy the look.

  831. Sent to me for review this product is very similar to mascara in that it aims to improve the appearance of your eyelashes by making them fuller, thicker and longer. This is meant to have the overall effect of making you look younger and sexier.<br /><br />Whilst applying standard mascara is generally a 1 step process involving just adding liquid to your eyelashes via a brush this product is totally different as it involves a 4 step process which actually involves using your own mascara as the 1st step.<br /><br />To summarise the steps you firstly add your own mascara and leave it to dry, you then add the transplanting gel to your lashes and then apply the natural fibres to your eyelashes whilst the gel is wet. You then reapply the transplanting gel onto the eyelashes to secure it all together.<br /><br />The product comes impressively presented in a smart retro case (similar size to prescription spectacles case) and has inside it the gel and fibres in a pen sized tube which are in fact a similar size to mascara. They come with full instructions which are quite easy to follow but I personally found all the information on the product page, instructions and the additional instructions I received via E-Mail to overcomplicate the whole process.<br /><br />The results were good after the 1st application and were a lot better after the second application. It's also water proof and overall it worked well although I didn't expect customers to need to use their own mascara and for it to be a 4 step process. Certainly worth trying given that you have the free 30 day guarantee to fall back on.

  879. I couldn't believe the difference--my lashes are so short--and when I saw the pics I thought they must be putting it on over fales lashes. Then my sister tried the Younique brand and I saw first hand that it really does work. I've been using the Younique brand and love it but was looking for a less expensive alternative. I saw this brand and decided to give it a try. I find no difference between the two. The transplanting gel with both brands is very thick. I personally don't like it that thick so I add a few drops of saline solution (for contacts) and find it works much better. The real key to not having the fibers fall onto your face (or anywhere else) is to not let the transplanting gel dry. I put my base mascara on both eyes-top and bottom, then I put the gel on the top lashes of 1 eye and immediatly put on the fibers, then I do the bottom lashes of that eye. While those dry I do the other eye. If I want a longer look I repeat the process, if not then I just go over all of them with the gel again--make sure not to forget this step or you will have fibers falling off all day. If you do it right they will stay on all day. The only problem -and it is very minor-is that you really have to take it off every day. Once after I started using the fiber lashes, I got home late and did not take it off before I went to bed. I was short on time in the morning and tried to just put it on over what was there but it did not look good at all. It is not a problem with this brand it is the same with the other one--you just can't do &#34;second day&#34; with them--my lashes looked thick and goopy so I just make sure to take it off every night. I will never go back to regular mascara and will definitely buy this brand again!
